## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature constitutive relationship of a material, where stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic deformation mechanisms and on temperature through thermal softening and thermally activated processes.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small strain elastic behavior)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (c1 - T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic strain hardening, Hollomon equation)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * epsilon**c3) (elastic-plastic transition)
- Johnson-Cook strength model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T**c5) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Voce hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * (c3 - c4 * T) (saturating hardening)
- Arrhenius thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Ludwik equation with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (power hardening with Arrhenius softening)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic behavior)
- Linear thermal-mechanical coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T + c2 * epsilon * T (bilinear coupling)
- Hyperbolic sine flow stress: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Sellars-Tegart / Garofalo model)
- Rational softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * c2 / (c3 + T) (inverse temperature dependence)
- Sigmoidal strain response: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating stress with thermal softening)
- Zerilli-Armstrong BCC model: sigma = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * T) + c3 * epsilon**c4 (dislocation mechanics based)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening typically appears as a multiplicative factor that decreases with temperature, such as (1 - c*T**m) or exp(-c*T)
- Strain hardening in metals follows power-law form epsilon**n where n is between 0 and 1, reflecting dislocation accumulation
- Stress saturation at large strains suggests exponential approach forms like c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon))
- Elastic-to-plastic transition often manifests as additive terms: a linear epsilon term plus a power-law or saturating term
- Inverse temperature (c0/T) or Arrhenius (exp(-c0/T)) terms indicate thermally activated deformation mechanisms
- Strain-temperature cross terms (epsilon * T or epsilon * exp(c*T)) indicate that hardening rate itself depends on temperature
- A yield stress offset (additive constant c0) represents the temperature-dependent lattice friction or Peierls stress
- Melting/critical temperature effects appear as (T_m - T) factors where stress vanishes at a critical temperature
